<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hythe_RH%26DR_station_geograph-3277356-by-Ben-Brooksbank.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1441" data-file-width="2395" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Hythe_RH%26DR_station_geograph-3277356-by-Ben-Brooksbank.jpg/220px-Hythe_RH%26DR_station_geograph-3277356-by-Ben-Brooksbank.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Hythe_RH%26DR_station_geograph-3277356-by-Ben-Brooksbank.jpg/330px-Hythe_RH%26DR_station_geograph-3277356-by-Ben-Brooksbank.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Hythe_RH%26DR_station_geograph-3277356-by-Ben-Brooksbank.jpg/440px-Hythe_RH%26DR_station_geograph-3277356-by-Ben-Brooksbank.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hythe_RH%26DR_station_geograph-3277356-by-Ben-Brooksbank.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hythe station with train in 1962</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <b>Romney, Hythe &amp; Dymchurch Railway</b> (<b>RH&amp;DR</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Fifteen-inch_gauge_railway" title="Fifteen-inch gauge railway"><span class="nowrap">15 in</span></a> (<span class="nowrap">381 mm</span>) gauge <a href="/wiki/Light_railway" title="Light railway">light railway</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kent" title="Kent">Kent</a>, England, operating steam and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Internal_combustion" title="Internal combustion">internal combustion</a> locomotives. The <span class="frac nowrap">13<span class="visualhide"> </span><sup>3</sup>⁄<sub>4</sub></span>-mile (22.1 km) line runs from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cinque_Port" title="Cinque Port">Cinque Port</a> of <a href="/wiki/Hythe,_Kent" title="Hythe, Kent">Hythe</a> via <a href="/wiki/Dymchurch" title="Dymchurch">Dymchurch</a>, <a href="/wiki/St_Mary%27s_Bay,_Kent" title="St Mary's Bay, Kent">St. Mary's Bay</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Romney" title="New Romney">New Romney</a> and Romney Sands to <a href="/wiki/Dungeness_(headland)" title="Dungeness (headland)">Dungeness</a>, close to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dungeness_nuclear_power_station" title="Dungeness nuclear power station">Dungeness nuclear power station</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dungeness_Lighthouse" title="Dungeness Lighthouse">Dungeness Lighthouse</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Planning">Planning</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Planning">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The railway was the dream of millionaire racing drivers Captain John Edwards Presgrave ("Jack") Howey and <a href="/wiki/Louis_Zborowski" title="Louis Zborowski">Count Louis Zborowski</a>. The latter had constructed a railway at <a href="/wiki/Higham_Park" title="Higham Park">Higham Park</a>, his home at <a href="/wiki/Bridge,_Kent" title="Bridge, Kent">Bridge, Kent</a>, and agreed to donate the rolling stock and infrastructure to the project. However, he was killed on 19 October 1924 in a motor racing accident at <a href="/wiki/Autodromo_Nazionale_Monza" title="Autodromo Nazionale Monza">the Monza</a> Grand Prix before the Romney Marsh site was chosen, and Howey continued the project alone.</p>
<p>After Howey had unsuccessfully attempted to buy the Ravenglass &amp; Eskdale Railway and extend it, he investigated a greenfield site between Burnham-on-Sea and Weston-super-Mare in Somerset and offered to buy the Hundred of Manhood &amp; Selsey Tramway in Sussex, <a href="/wiki/Henry_Greenly" title="Henry Greenly">Henry Greenly</a> drew Howey's attention to the potential for a 15-inch gauge line between New Romney and Hythe. Howey first visited New Romney on 8 September 1925 and decided there and then that it was an ideal location for his proposed railway.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Snell_1993_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-Snell_1993-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>Because it involved crossing public highways and acquiring land from a number of different owners a Light Railway Order made under the Light Railways Act 1896 was necessary and application for this was made in November 1925. A Public Inquiry was held by the Light Railway Commissioners in the Assembly Rooms at New Romney on 15 and 16 January 1926.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> The Minister of Transport indicated his intention to approve the application on 19 February 1926 and The Romney, Hythe &amp; Dymchurch Light Railway Order 1926 was made on 26 May.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> This incorporated the Romney, Hythe &amp; Dymchurch Light Railway Company as a statutory public utility undertaking, gave it powers to construct and work the proposed railway and also included compulsory purchase powers over the land required (which ultimately had to be used to acquire six plots of land on the proposed route).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Snell_1993_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-Snell_1993-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>During construction, the railway was visited on 5 August 1926 by the Duke of York, (later <a href="/wiki/George_VI" title="George VI">King George VI</a>), who drove the Northern Chief hauling a train of approximately 100 passengers from Jesson Halt to New Romney and back.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Opening">Opening</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Opening">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The railway was opened on 16 July 1927 by <a href="/wiki/Lord_Warden_of_the_Cinque_Ports" title="Lord Warden of the Cinque Ports">Lord Warden of the Cinque Ports</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Lygon,_7th_Earl_Beauchamp" title="William Lygon, 7th Earl Beauchamp">William Lygon, 7th Earl Beauchamp</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> The locomotives were designed by Henry Greenly who was commissioned by Howey to work on the construction of the entire railway <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> and became the railway's first chief engineer until his abrupt resignation in March 1929.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Snell_1993_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-Snell_1993-1">[1]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/4-8-2" title="4-8-2">Mountain Class</a> <i>Hercules</i> hauled the inaugural train from Hythe to New Romney, with guests including the mayors of the two towns and General Sir <a href="/wiki/Ivor_Maxse" title="Ivor Maxse">Ivor Maxse</a>.</p>
<p>Howey was not satisfied with just <span class="frac nowrap">8<span class="visualhide"> </span><sup>1</sup>⁄<sub>4</sub></span> miles (13.3 km) of track from Hythe to New Romney and plans were in hand for an extension even before the original section had opened. The line was to be extended <span class="frac nowrap">5<span class="visualhide"> </span><sup>1</sup>⁄<sub>2</sub></span> miles (9 km) from New Romney to Dungeness, double-tracked throughout apart from a balloon loop on which the station at Dungeness was sited. A Light Railway Order for this extension was applied for and, following a Public Inquiry on 18 April 1928, the Romney, Hythe &amp; Dymchurch Light Railway (Extension) Order was granted on 12 July 1928. Ahead of this the line between New Romney and The Pilot had actually opened on 24 May 1928 and the rest of the line through to Dungeness opened on 3 August 1928.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> Since it was laid directly onto the shingle forming the Dungeness peninsula it has been suggested that the extension was the most cheaply constructed railway in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Davies_1988_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Davies_1988-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_World_War">Second World War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Second World War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The railway was taken over by the military during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, and a miniature <a href="/wiki/Armoured_train" title="Armoured train">armoured train</a> was used on the line.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-liberalengland.blogspot.com_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-liberalengland.blogspot.com-9">[9]</a></sup> It was also used by the Department of Petroleum Warfare in the construction of <a href="/wiki/Operation_Pluto" title="Operation Pluto">PLUTO</a> ("Pipe Line Under The Ocean") intended to supply fuel to the Allied forces after the D-Day Normandy landings. During the latter stages of the construction of PLUTO considerable damage was caused to the track on the extension when, to speed up the work, lengths of pipe were dragged along the trackbed by bulldozers, resulting in its reduction to a single track after the war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Snell_1993_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-Snell_1993-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post_war">Post war</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Post war">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The line re-opened between Hythe and New Romney in 1946, the New Romney to Dungeness section following with a formal opening by <a href="/wiki/Laurel_and_Hardy" title="Laurel and Hardy">Laurel and Hardy</a> on 21 March 1947.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Regular services started on 29 March 1947.</p>
<p>In June 1947 the <a href="/wiki/Eaton_Hall_Railway" title="Eaton Hall Railway">Duke of Westminster’s railway</a> from <a href="/wiki/Eaton_Hall,_Cheshire" title="Eaton Hall, Cheshire">Eaton Hall, Cheshire</a> was transported by the <a href="/wiki/Great_Western_Railway" title="Great Western Railway">Great Western Railway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southern_Railway_(UK)" title="Southern Railway (UK)">Southern Railway</a> from <a href="/wiki/Balderton,_Cheshire" title="Balderton, Cheshire">Balderton, Cheshire</a> to <a href="/wiki/New_Romney" title="New Romney">New Romney</a> in Kent. It comprised an engine, nine coaches and trucks, and track totalling 222 tons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1949, Captain Howey bought the Duke of Sutherland's private train including engine <a href="/wiki/Dunrobin_(locomotive)" title="Dunrobin (locomotive)">Dunrobin</a> and 60 feet (18 m) coach for the museum at New Romney. It was transported there in 1950<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> and displayed until sold in 1963.</p>
<p>From 7 September 1977 until 24 July 2015, the railway provided school trains to transport children to and from the <a href="/wiki/Marsh_Academy" title="Marsh Academy">Marsh Academy</a> in New Romney. The service was finally withdrawn due to falling usage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>The railway's role as part of the local public transport network was extended when <a href="/wiki/Warren_Halt_railway_station" title="Warren Halt railway station">Warren Halt</a> re-opened in 2009, providing a link to the Romney Marsh Visitor Centre. Further discussions with local councils took place regarding the possible expansion of <a href="/wiki/Burmarsh_Road_railway_station" title="Burmarsh Road railway station">Burmarsh Road</a> and the provision of a new station at the gravel pits in West Hythe, in connection with both the proposed extensive new housing construction and the need to provide alternative transport to the <a href="/wiki/A259_road" title="A259 road">A259</a> coast road.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>The railway, which carries over 150,000 passengers each year,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> celebrated its 80th birthday in 2007 with a week of celebrations including reconstructions of scenes on the railway from the previous eight decades.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Smallest_public_railway_in_the_world">Smallest public railway in the world</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Smallest public railway in the world">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From 1926 to 1978, the RH&amp;DR held the title of the "Smallest public railway in the world" (in terms of track gauge). The title was lost to the <span class="nowrap"><span class="frac">12<span class="visualhide"> </span><sup>1</sup>⁄<sub>4</sub></span> in</span> (<span class="nowrap">311 mm</span>) gauge <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9seau_Guerl%C3%A9dan" title="Réseau Guerlédan">Réseau Guerlédan</a> in <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> in 1978<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-World-16">[16]</a></sup> and regained in 1979 when that line closed. It was lost again in 1982 when the <span class="nowrap"><span class="frac">10<span class="visualhide"> </span><sup>1</sup>⁄<sub>4</sub></span> in</span> (<span class="nowrap">260 mm</span>) gauge <a href="/wiki/Wells_and_Walsingham_Light_Railway" title="Wells and Walsingham Light Railway">Wells and Walsingham Light Railway</a> opened.</p>
<p>The railway has featured in several television and radio shows including an episode of the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> series <i><a href="/wiki/The_Inspector_Lynley_Mysteries" title="The Inspector Lynley Mysteries">The Inspector Lynley Mysteries</a></i> in 2006,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Harry Secombe's <i>Highway</i> on 8 September 1991,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Michael_Bentine" title="Michael Bentine">Michael Bentine</a>'s <i>It's a Square World</i> in 1964,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> BBC's Multicoloured Swapshop (filmed on 20 February 1978) <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> and children's show <a href="/wiki/Rainbow_(TV_series)" title="Rainbow (TV series)"><i>Rainbow</i></a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span id="The_Romney,_Hythe_&amp;_Dymchurch_Railway_Association"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Romney.2C_Hythe_.26_Dymchurch_Railway_Association">The Romney, Hythe &amp; Dymchurch Railway Association</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: The Romney, Hythe &amp; Dymchurch Railway Association">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Formed in 1967 as a supporters association, and regarded with some suspicion by the railway's management of the time, the association has become a significant contributor to the railway's continuance and refurbishment. It is now the largest single shareholder in the railway and its members provide a significant input of voluntary labour on both operating and maintenance work.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (September 2016)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup> It became a registered charity on 23 January 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> At 31 December 2015 its membership stood at 3,355.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Stations">Stations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Stations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stations_currently_open">Stations currently open</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Stations currently open">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Stations in full or limited use:</p>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hythe_railway_station_(RHDR)" title="Hythe railway station (RHDR)">Hythe</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Burmarsh_Road_railway_station" title="Burmarsh Road railway station">Burmarsh Road</a> (usually special services only)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dymchurch_railway_station" title="Dymchurch railway station">Dymchurch</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/St_Mary%27s_Bay_railway_station" title="St Mary's Bay railway station">St Mary's Bay</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Warren_Halt_railway_station" title="Warren Halt railway station">Warren Halt</a> (usually visitor centre shuttle trains only)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/New_Romney_railway_station" title="New Romney railway station">New Romney</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Romney_Sands_railway_station" title="Romney Sands railway station">Romney Sands</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dungeness_railway_station" title="Dungeness railway station">Dungeness</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stations_closed">Stations closed</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Stations closed">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Those shown as 'halt' never had a higher status; all stations below became halts prior to their closure.</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Wales_Halt_railway_station" title="Prince of Wales Halt railway station">Prince of Wales Halt</a> (closed 1928)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Botolph%27s_Bridge_Halt_railway_station" title="Botolph's Bridge Halt railway station">Botolph's Bridge Halt</a> (closed 1939)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Golden_Sands_Halt_railway_station" title="Golden Sands Halt railway station">Golden Sands Halt</a> (closed 1990s)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Greatstone_Dunes_railway_station" title="Greatstone Dunes railway station">Greatstone</a> (closed 1983)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/War_Department_Halt_railway_station" title="War Department Halt railway station">War Department Halt</a> (closed 1945)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lade_railway_station" title="Lade railway station">Lade</a> (closed 1983)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/The_Pilot_Inn_railway_station" title="The Pilot Inn railway station">The Pilot Inn</a> (closed 1983)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Britannia_Points_Halt_railway_station" title="Britannia Points Halt railway station">Britannia Points Halt</a> (closed 1930)</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stations_proposed">Stations proposed</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Stations proposed">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Stations which never existed but were at one time proposed by the directors or are currently under consideration:</p>
<ul>
<li>Hythe (Red Lion Square): Was first mentioned at the January 1928 meeting of Hythe Chamber of Commerce by Charles Duruz, a local nurseryman, who had contacted the railway company and who indicated they were quite willing to build this extension. Nothing came of the proposal however.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> In 1946 the possibility of extending the railway to Red Lion Square, Hythe was investigated again, but the East Kent Road Car Co Ltd agreed to extend their bus service from Folkestone to terminate at the original Hythe station and the extension idea was dropped.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morris.2C_1946_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Morris.2C_1946-24">[24]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sandling_Junction_railway_station_(RHDR)" title="Sandling Junction railway station (RHDR)">Sandling Junction</a>: Suggested by objectors to the railway's original Light Railway Order in 1926 as more useful than a terminus on the outskirts of Hythe, but demonstrated by Greenly to be impracticable because of the difference in levels between Hythe and Sandling which would have necessitated severe gradients.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Davies_1988_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-Davies_1988-8">[8]</a></sup> The idea was revived in the late 1980s to connect with the main line at Sandling but again came to nothing, although detailed survey work had been undertaken.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sandling_Park_railway_station" title="Sandling Park railway station">Sandling Park</a>: A proposal was made for a station to serve this estate at <a href="/wiki/Pedlinge" title="Pedlinge">Pedlinge</a> on the abortive 1980s Sandling extension.</li>
<li>Nickolls Quarry: A proposal for a station to serve a new housing development at the West Hythe site of Nickolls Quarry has been formally included in a planning application to <a href="/wiki/Shepway" title="Shepway">Shepway</a> District Council.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></li>
</ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Way_and_Works">Way and Works</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Way and Works">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Permanent_Way">Permanent Way</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Permanent Way">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The line was originally laid using second-hand First World War surplus rail. Most was 25 lb/yd material rolled in the USA, the rest was 12 kg/m rolled in Belgium when the country was under German occupation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Snell.2C_1993_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Snell.2C_1993-26">[26]</a></sup> In the late 1960s and early 1970s the railway managed to obtain supplies of good second-hand 30 lb/yd rail on the closure of the Sierra Leone Government Railway;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Snell.2C_1993_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-Snell.2C_1993-26">[26]</a></sup> these are the oldest rails on the line, some of which date from the 1890s.</p>
<p>During the mid-1980s the company began obtaining brand new 25 lb/yd rail from Luxembourg before switching to 30 lb/yd material produced British Steel Track Products in Scunthorpe and later obtained further supplies of the same from South Africa. The present standard rail for re-laying work is 35 lb/yd obtained from a manufacturer in Spain.</p>
<p>The original sleepers were creosoted Baltic fir spaced at 22 inch centres.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morris.2C_1946_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-Morris.2C_1946-24">[24]</a></sup> These have now been entirely replaced by second-hand standard gauge sleepers cut into thirds, creosoted douglas fir, or jarrah and karri (Australian hardwoods from the eucalyptus family).</p>
<p>The railway has a Permanent Way team, with a full-time staff of <a href="/wiki/Platelayer" title="Platelayer">platelayers</a>. It forms part of the larger Engineering Department. Some platelayers work all year round, whilst others are diverted to other seasonal employment within the engineering department, for example as summer drivers, when more drivers are required than during the out of season periods. Additionally, the permanent way team is strengthened on many days of the year, especially in the winter months, by volunteer workers.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Way_and_works_data">Way and works data</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Way and works data">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The longest underline bridge is Collins Bridge, with a span of approximately 60 ft.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Snell.2C_1993_26-2"><a href="#cite_note-Snell.2C_1993-26">[26]</a></sup> The summit of the line is 20 ft above Ordnance Datum, located between Hull Road and Taylor Road, Lydd-on–Sea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> The ruling gradient is 1 in 75 at the Dungeness end of New Romney Station rising from the Littlestone Road Tunnels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> The tightest curve measures 6.8 chains radius and is at the Hythe end of 'The Deviation', a <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Dogleg" title="Dogleg">dogleg</a><sup class="plainlinks noprint Inline-Template" style="vertical-align:text-top;white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="external text" href="http://dispenser.info.tm/~dispenser/cgi-bin/dab_solver.py?page=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;editintro=Template:Disambiguation_needed/editintro&amp;client=Template:Dn" rel="nofollow"><span title="Link needs disambiguation. (November 2016)">disambiguation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> section of track at <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Pennypot&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Pennypot (page does not exist)">Pennypot</a> on the outskirts of Hythe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>The ruling gradient and tightest curve are the results of post-1972 reconstruction work. Pre-1990 references to these give out of date figures. Statements in a number of books claiming the summit of the line is at Star Dyke (a point approximately midway between Burmarsh Road level crossing and Willop Sewer) are only partly correct; whilst it is the highest point between Hythe and New Romney <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> it is not the highest on the entire line.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Signalling">Signalling</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Signalling">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Signal_boxes">Signal boxes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Signal boxes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There were originally six signal boxes on the first section of the line to open (Hythe to New Romney). All were equipped with Greenly designed fully interlocked lever frames constructed by Jackson Rigby Ltd at New Romney. These were:</p>
<p><b>Hythe</b> - 16 levers controlling points and signals within the station area. Now the only original Jackson Rigby lever frame in existence.</p>
<p><b>Palmarsh</b> - although this building is known to have existed there is doubt about whether the 8 lever Jackson Rigby frame it contained was ever fully connected up. The frame was later transferred to Greatstone (see below). The box itself had vanished by the late-1940s.</p>
<p><b>Burmarsh Road</b> - 2 levers located in the booking office and controlling signals. The station building had vanished by the mid-1950s.</p>
<p><b>Dymchurch</b> - confusion surrounds the number of levers in this box, with different sources quoting 10,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> 12 <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> and 16.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> The box had vanished by 1963 and signalling is controlled here today by a push button electronic panel in the booking office and a 2 lever ground frame released by an <a href="/wiki/Annett%27s_key" title="Annett's key">Annett's key</a> normally held in the signal panel.</p>
<p><b>Holiday Camp</b> – this building is known to have been erected on land owned by Allnatt Ltd since it is marked on the plans accompanying a combined conveyance/lease concluded by the railway with that company and is shown as measuring 12 ft by 6 ft.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Some rather poor quality photographic evidence of the existence of this box also exists. There is uncertainty as to whether it was ever brought into use though and if so how many levers it contained.</p>
<p><b>New Romney</b> – 17 levers controlling points and signals within the station area. The lever frame was enlarged to the present 24 levers when the line was extended to Dungeness in 1928.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morris.2C_1946_24-2"><a href="#cite_note-Morris.2C_1946-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>The extension to Dungeness led to the enlargement of the lever frame at New Romney (as mentioned above) and also the opening of two new signal boxes:</p>
<p><b>Greatstone</b> - the 8 lever frame originally at Palmarsh was transferred here and installed in the booking office.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p><b>Dungeness</b> - like Dymchurch it is uncertain how many levers this box actually contained.</p>
<p>Arrangements for working the temporary turning wye at <b>The Pilot</b> are not known.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Locomotives">Locomotives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Locomotives">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>All ten original steam locomotives remain in service, each covering up to 10,000 miles (16,000 km) a year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>The fleet, already the largest of any 15-inch (380 mm) railway in Britain,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Snell_1993_1-4"><a href="#cite_note-Snell_1993-1">[1]</a></sup> was expanded in 1976 with the addition of German-built Krupp locomotive No 11 <i>Black Prince</i> (formerly <i>Fleißiges Lieschen</i> (<i>Busy Lizzie</i>)).</p>
<p>The RH&amp;DR is still the only user of the <a href="/wiki/4-8-2" title="4-8-2">4-8-2</a> Mountain type locomotive in the UK, with No 6 <i>Samson</i> and No 5 <i>Hercules</i> in regular service.</p>
<p>The fleet includes two diesels, No 12 <i>J B Snell</i> (delivered in February 1983, and renamed from its original <i>John Southland</i> in May 2014) and No 14 (delivered November 1989, and later named <i>Captain Howey</i>).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Locomotives_in_service">Locomotives in service</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Locomotives in service">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<td align="center">14</td>
<td align="center"><i>Captain Howey</i></td>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Locomotive_names">Locomotive names</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Locomotive names">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>Nameplates are usually in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Upper_case" title="Upper case">upper case</a>.</li>
<li>No 1 was named <i>Green Goddess</i> after the 1921 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Green_Goddess_(stage_play)" title="The Green Goddess (stage play)">stage play</a> by <a href="/wiki/William_Archer_(critic)" title="William Archer (critic)">William Archer</a>, which Captain Howey had enjoyed.</li>
<li>Nos 2 &amp; 3 were to be called <i>Northern Chief</i> and <i>Southern Chief</i> and these nameplates were fitted at the works; however No 3's name was changed to <i>Southern Maid</i>.</li>
<li>No 4 was sold in 1934 after construction because the proposed shunting and freight trains for it to work did not materialise. It ran in <a href="/wiki/Belle_Vue,_Manchester" title="Belle Vue, Manchester">Belle Vue, Manchester</a>, then <a href="/wiki/Belfast" title="Belfast">Belfast</a> with the new name <i>Jean</i>. The engine regained its original name on return to the RH&amp;DR and restoration in the 1970s. It bears the colloquial name <i>Basil the Bug</i> in its role as mascot of the railway's children's supporter group.</li>
<li>Nos 5 &amp; 6 were to be called <i>Man of Kent</i> and <i>Maid of Kent</i>, but due to their high tractive effort (having smaller coupled wheels than the Pacifics) the names <i><a href="/wiki/Hercules" title="Hercules">Hercules</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Samson" title="Samson">Samson</a></i>, with their allusion of strength, were substituted during construction. A decade later, <a href="/wiki/Henry_Greenly" title="Henry Greenly">Henry Greenly</a>, the designer, was involved in the construction of a locomotive on the nearby <a href="/wiki/Saltwood_Miniature_Railway" title="Saltwood Miniature Railway">Saltwood Miniature Railway</a>, and this engine took the <i>Maid of Kent</i> name.</li>
<li>Nos 7 &amp; 8 were constructed with an extra third cylinder for express passenger services and were given their names <i>Typhoon</i> and <i>Hurricane</i> for speed. The third cylinder was later removed from each due to unreliability. The locomotives were originally to carry the <i>Samson</i> and <i>Hercules</i> nameplates, but Howey gave the Mountain classes these names before the three-cylinder locomotives had arrived.</li>
<li>Following a mishap when Howey was at the controls, No 8 was renamed <i>Bluebottle</i> between 1938 and 1946, apparently as a punishment.</li>
<li>No 9 was originally <i>Black Prince</i>, but exchanged its name with No 10 in 1931. its name became <i><a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a></i> in 1948 for a tour of Canada, and remained so afterwards. At the same time the name <i>Doctor Syn</i> was transferred to No 10 and the name <i>Black Prince</i> fell into disuse.</li>
<li>No 10 was originally <i>Doctor Syn</i>, but was renamed <i>Black Prince</i> following an accident in 1931. It regained its original name in 1949 to maintain the link with local history and legend.</li>
<li>A brass name plate survives suggesting one of the Canadian outline locos was originally to have been called <i>Black Devil</i>. In the event this name was never used. George Barlow, the railway's operating manager, received a brass rubbing of this from an enquirer. When offered up to the cab side of <i>Doctor Syn</i> the bolt holes on the rubbing matched those in the loco's cab side perfectly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></li>
<li>Some confusion exists over which locomotive actually carried the name <i>Doctor Syn</i> at any particular time. If the real <i>Doctor Syn</i> was out of service for any reason Howey often had its nameplates switched onto the other Canadian outline locomotive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></li>
<li>No 11 took over the redundant <i>Black Prince</i> name upon transfer to the RH&amp;DR in 1976, in place of its German name <i>Fleißiges Lieschen</i> (Busy Lizzie). The name was chosen after a competition run by a local newspaper in which <i>Spitfire</i> scored heavily, but was considered rather undiplomatic given the loco's origins. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Snell_1993_1-5"><a href="#cite_note-Snell_1993-1">[1]</a></sup></li>
<li>No 12, originally named <i>John Southland</i> after the founder of the local secondary school in New Romney, has since been renamed after the railway's long serving managing director John Bernard Snell.</li>
<li>No 13 was never assigned, probably due to superstition. Another engine of the same class as Nos 12 and 14 was built in the years between them and exported to the <a href="/wiki/Shuzenji_Romney_Railway" title="Shuzenji Romney Railway">Shuzenji Romney Railway</a> in Japan where it is No 3 in their fleet and carries the name <i>John Southland II</i>.</li>
<li>No 14 ran nameless for 12 years until it was named after the line's founder, Captain Howey.</li>
<li>PW1 carried the fleet number 4 for about ten years from 1961 as a replacement for the <a href="/wiki/Rolls-Royce_Holdings" title="Rolls-Royce Holdings">Rolls-Royce</a> engine, which in turn had inherited the number from <i>The Bug</i> which had been sold. The engine was renumbered PW1 shortly before the return of <i>The Bug</i>, leaving fleet number 4 available again for its original holder.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></li>
<li>PW2 was constructed in 1949, mainly by the rebuilding and re-use of a former War Department locomotive which had been in service since 1929. Popularly known as <i>The Scooter</i> it has recently acquired nameplates showing this name.</li>
<li>PW3 <i>Redgauntlet</i> was built c1964 by Michel Jacot and using a modified Austin 7 engine originally ran on paraffin. It ran trials at both the Ravenglass &amp; Eskdale and Romney, Hythe &amp; Dymchurch in the late 1960s and was acquired by the RHDR in the early 1970s.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Locomotives_withdrawn_from_service">Locomotives withdrawn from service</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Locomotives withdrawn from service">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
