<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Locomotives_on_site">Locomotives on site</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Locomotives on site">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In addition to the railway's 17 own locomotives, one additional engine is currently housed at New Romney. This is a partially constructed third-scale reproduction of an <a href="/wiki/London,_Midland_and_Scottish_Railway" title="London, Midland and Scottish Railway">LMS</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Princess_Coronation_Class" title="Princess Coronation Class">Princess Coronation Class</a> locomotive, commonly known as the 'Duchess' type (although of the 38 engines of this class, only 10 were named after <a href="/wiki/Duke" title="Duke">duchesses</a>). The replica was commissioned by Paul Riley, a director of the railway, as a private project and is currently stored in an engineers' depot.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> Following the unexpected death of Mr Riley on 4 June 2008 the future of this locomotive is currently unknown. It is understood that the machine is more than half complete.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Passenger_traffic">Passenger traffic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Passenger traffic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Passenger_services">Passenger services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Passenger services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The railway was conceived and constructed as a public service, not as a tourist attraction, although it now relies on tourist trade.</p>
<p>School children were transported under contract to <a href="/wiki/Kent_County_Council" title="Kent County Council">Kent County Council</a> to <a class="external text" href="http://www.marshacademy.org.uk" rel="nofollow">The Marsh Academy</a> (known as <i>Southland's Comprehensive School</i> until 2007); this service was provided all year during term time. The contract ceased due to falling passenger numbers after the summer term in July 2015. Local residents are transported to shopping centres and the railway has operated 'shoppers specials'. <a href="/wiki/Holiday_camp" title="Holiday camp">Holiday camp</a> trains have operated with camps at Romney Sands, St Mary's Bay and Dymchurch. Charters are operated as required. During the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">Second World War</a> the railway was operated by The Royal Engineers and later the <a href="/wiki/Somerset_Light_Infantry" title="Somerset Light Infantry">Somerset Light Infantry</a> as a military railway and there was extensive transport of soldiers on troop trains.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Passenger_vehicles">Passenger vehicles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Passenger vehicles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>At the outset the railway was equipped with four-wheeled 8-seater coaches designed by Henry Greenly and his son Kenneth. 117 of these had been built by 1928.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Snell_1993_1-6"><a href="#cite_note-Snell_1993-1">[1]</a></sup> With only half height doors and no glazing except in the end bulkheads these were totally unsuitable for winter operation, especially to Dungeness. In 1928 the railway took delivery of eight fully enclosed 12-seat bogie coaches built by the Clayton Carriage &amp; Wagon Company of Lincoln which incorporated electric lighting and steam heating.</p>
<p>In 1934 Howey decided to scrap all the original four-wheelers and replace them with fully enclosed bogie vehicles. The 16 foot underframes for these were constructed by Robert Hudson Ltd of Leeds and the bodies were built locally by the Hythe Cabinet &amp; Joinery Works Ltd. By June 1936 54 of these together with two matching vans had been taken into stock.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Snell_1993_1-7"><a href="#cite_note-Snell_1993-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>The RH&amp;DR now operates 20-seat and 16-seat open and closed coaches. These have been built on four different types of underframe:</p>
<ul>
<li>The original <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Clayton_Carriage_%26_Wagon_Co&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Clayton Carriage &amp; Wagon Co (page does not exist)">Clayton Carriage &amp; Wagon Co</a> 20 ft 3 in (6.17 m) long frames unaltered in length (used for 16-seat opens and 8-seat guards vans)</li>
<li>The 1936 16 ft (4.88 m) Robert Hudson frames extended to between 23 ft 3 in (7.09 m) and 23 ft 9 in (7.24 m) by inserting a new centre section between the swan-necks which carry the frame over the bogies (used for 20-seat open and closed coaches)</li>
<li>A small batch of all welded 19 ft 9 in (6.02 m) long frames made by Gowers of Bedford in 1962 and unaltered in length (used for 16-seat closed coaches)</li>
<li>The remaining bogie hopper wagons acquired secondhand from the Ravenglass &amp; Eskdale Railway in 1928 (used for 20-seater semi-open coaches)</li>
</ul>
<p>The first batch of 20-seater closed coaches were bodied with utile (an African hardwood - pronounced "you-till-eye") and numbered 51 to 61 inclusive. From coach 62 onwards aluminium has been used.</p>
<p>Over 80 years the coach livery has changed from all-over green to brown and cream, blue, blue and cream, green and cream, chocolate and cream, and red and cream in the late 1980s. From 2000, rakes of coaches (trains of around a dozen coaches) have been painted in individual liveries and there are now maroon, green, blue, crimson and teak coaches; 'Heritage' coaches are chocolate and cream.</p>
<p>The railway has built several coaches to accommodate wheelchair users, starting with driving trailer coach 105 (heavily re-built after extensive accident damage in 1993 and later named <i>Marjorie</i>) followed by 601 <i>Elsie</i>, then 602 <i>Winn</i> and 603 <i>May</i>.</p>
<p>A new coach design featuring a lower floor, for easier loading, and a higher roof-line, giving better headroom for wheelchair users, was introduced in 2015. The first, <i>Phylis</i>, is painted lined brown and normally runs with the teak coaches. Two further coaches, <i>Iris</i> for the green set and <i>Edith May</i> for the teak/chocolate set, are under construction and will carry batteries in a compartment over one end bogie for coach lighting. As well as the wheelchair compartment, which has tip-up seats, each will have a guard's compartment with (emergency) brake valve, vacuum gauge, side ducket lookouts and a standard seating compartment. The guard's compartment has four seats and may be used by passengers when not in use by the guard</p>
<p>In addition to the main stock, the 'Heritage' set is made up of:</p>
<ul>
<li>the Clayton Pullman (built in 1928 and the last remaining example of a set of eight, with superior comfort and design with twelve seats in three compartments, originally with steam heating and coach lighting);</li>
<li>a preserved 1960s twelve-seat hardboard bodied coach named <i>Ruth;</i></li>
<li>the Royal Saloon (used by Queen Elizabeth II and members of her family when she visited the railway on 30 March 1957<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup>), a luxury version of a coach design introduced in 1934/5;</li>
<li>and the licensed bar car named <i>Gladys</i> (after Captain Howey's wife), an observation coach built on a 1936 Robert Hudson underframe extended to 32 ft (9.75 m) with a bar and 16 seats.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Freight_traffic">Freight traffic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Freight traffic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Freight_services">Freight services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Freight services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From the outset, the railway's owners and designers envisaged freight services. Two of the original locomotives (No 5 <i>Hercules</i> and No 6 <i>Samson</i>) were built to the 'mountain' wheel arrangement (<a href="/wiki/4-8-2" title="4-8-2">4-8-2</a>), unique on any British railway and giving the ability to haul heavy freight with only a small loss of speed when used on passenger work. In the early years the railway carried a limited amount of freight (mainly <a href="/wiki/Shingle_beach" title="Shingle beach">shingle</a> and fish traffic). A goods shed was built at New Romney and featured dual gauge track allowing easy transfer between the standard and 15 inch gauges. This was seldom used and was demolished in about 1934.</p>
<p>The greater part of the railway's freight traffic in the early years was carried for the War Department, who made extensive use of the line to convey materials and equipment for the construction of the reinforced concrete sound ranging detectors they were experimenting with near Greatstone. A special siding was laid in joining their working site with the RHDR main line (the course of which can still be traced today [2016]) and the WD constructed their own locomotive to work their trains.</p>
<p>From time to time, the railway has had short term <i>ad hoc</i> freight contracts, for example one in 1975 to transport drainage pipes. The most recent freight workings involved delivering gas mains from New Romney to Greatstone in 1989. As a publicity stunt the first gas main train was steam hauled using No 4 <i>The Bug</i>, which appeared on the local TV news that evening.</p>
<p>The railway operates its own engineering and <a href="/wiki/Track_(rail_transport)" title="Track (rail transport)">permanent way</a> trains, which now form the majority of its non-passenger workings.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Dungeness_fish_trade">Dungeness fish trade</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Dungeness fish trade">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>There are several disused sidings on the beach at Dungeness. These were used by fishermen to help move their hauls across the shingle. This joint provision was to allow transport of fish from Dungeness to Hythe and there to transfer it to road. The company had four-wheel fish wagons, stencilled "Fish Only". The service was developed from 1937 following closure of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_Eastern_Railway_(UK)" title="South Eastern Railway (UK)">South Eastern Railway</a>'s Dungeness line that year. The fish trade developed in a small way and was withdrawn. Two such sidings are still in place but are both in a very poor state of repair although they were used by fishermen to transport fish across the beach for many years after the main railway service was withdrawn.</p>
<p>To facilitate the transfer of this traffic from rail to road on its arrival at Hythe the track serving Platform 1 there extended into the car park for some years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Davies_1988_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-Davies_1988-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Uncrushed_shingle_transport">Uncrushed shingle transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Uncrushed shingle transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The most successful freight service was the uncrushed ballast service. Following withdrawal of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/War_Department" title="War Department">War Department</a> operations over their siding near Maddieson's Camp, the railway utilised the infrastructure to operate ballast trains. In 1937 a subsidiary ballast company was formed. <a href="/wiki/Dump_truck" title="Dump truck">Tipper</a> wagons (skips) were loaded with shingle and transported along the branch line and then up the main line to Hythe, often lying over in the sidings at Dymchurch to prevent delay to passenger trains using the same tracks. At Hythe the wagons were originally pushed by the locomotive up a concrete ramp and the wagons tipped into a large concrete holding bin or directly into waiting lorries, a precarious practice which was later replaced by mechanical haulage up the ramp. After the war the Hythe workings were cut back and the wagons were unloaded in a siding (in what is now New Romney station car park), the remnant of which is now used for loading coal into loco tenders. This practice didn't last long and a purpose built siding and ramp was installed south of New Romney on the Dungeness line. The fence line can still be seen. In 1951, after 14 years, the subsidiary company switched to entirely road transport and the company closed the branch and the freight incline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Snell_1993_1-8"><a href="#cite_note-Snell_1993-1">[1]</a></sup> At Hythe, the concrete pillars were still visible until the early 1980s when they were demolished to allow access to the car park extension along the former platform 4 and engine release siding.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Postal_service">Postal service</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Postal service">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The railway is licensed by <a href="/wiki/Royal_Mail" title="Royal Mail">the Post Office</a> for rail postal services, and is entitled to issue postage stamps. A number of <a href="/wiki/First_day_of_issue" title="First day of issue">first day covers</a> have been issued. A four-wheel secure postage wagon was constructed.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Parcels_service">Parcels service</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Parcels service">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The railway operates a casual parcels service. Parcels handed in at one station will be delivered to another for collection. This is the last remnant of the railway's freight services.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:100_1588_(Medium).JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/100_1588_%28Medium%29.JPG/220px-100_1588_%28Medium%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/100_1588_%28Medium%29.JPG/330px-100_1588_%28Medium%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/100_1588_%28Medium%29.JPG/440px-100_1588_%28Medium%29.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:100_1588_(Medium).JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Some of the freight wagons behind No 2</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Freight_vehicles">Freight vehicles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Freight vehicles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The railway has permanent way stock, examples of which include:</p>
<ul>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Platelayer" title="Platelayer">platelayers</a>' mess coach 100P</li>
<li>assorted tipper wagons (largely left over from ballast operations)</li>
<li>secure tool trucks</li>
<li>specialized platelaying vehicles incorporating concrete mixers, compressors, generators etc.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Flatcar" title="Flatcar">flat wagons</a></li>
<li>four-wheel wagons, both box vans and open trucks, including vehicles surviving from the fish trains</li>
<li>tank wagons, used primarily for spraying weed killer on tracks.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Armoured_train">Armoured train</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Armoured train">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_armoured_train.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="605" data-file-width="800" height="189" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Romney%2C_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_armoured_train.jpg/250px-Romney%2C_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_armoured_train.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Romney%2C_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_armoured_train.jpg/375px-Romney%2C_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_armoured_train.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Romney%2C_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_armoured_train.jpg/500px-Romney%2C_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_armoured_train.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_armoured_train.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Romney, Hythe and Dymchurch Railway armoured train, October 1940</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During World War II, a miniature <a href="/wiki/Armoured_train" title="Armoured train">armoured train</a> was used on the line to patrol the coast in case of invasion. The train was armed with a <a href="/wiki/Boys_anti-tank_rifle" title="Boys anti-tank rifle">Boys anti-tank rifle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lewis_gun" title="Lewis gun">Lewis guns</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-liberalengland.blogspot.com_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-liberalengland.blogspot.com-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Proposed_extension_to_Sandling">Proposed extension to Sandling</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Proposed extension to Sandling">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Objectors to the railway's first Light Railway Order advocated an extension from Hythe to <a href="/wiki/Sandling" title="Sandling">Sandling</a> (2 miles (3.2 km) away) to meet mainline services at <a href="/wiki/Sandling_railway_station" title="Sandling railway station">Sandling Junction</a> which they claimed would provide a more useful transport facility than the original proposals. Henry Greenly undertook a preliminary survey which demonstrated the scheme was impracticable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>Supposition that the <a href="/wiki/4-8-2" title="4-8-2">4-8-2</a> locomotives <i>Hercules</i> and <i>Samson</i> were ordered for the project, which involved steep inclines, is unfounded as the engines were intended for freight traffic, in particular a contract with Kent County Council to transport up to 30,000 tons of ballast a year from their pits at Palmarsh. In the end this contract failed to materialize.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the 1980s, the directors reconsidered proposals to extend the line to Sandling and detailed surveys were undertaken. Again, consideration was given to motive power with new locomotives discussed. Although still called the "Sandling Extension", the 1980s plan was for a single-track line from Pennypot, 300 yards (270 m) short of Hythe, to provide a more gentle route to an area known as The Roughs, where a more powerful locomotive would take over for the heavy climb to Sandling station. It would therefore have been a branch line rather than an actual extension to the existing mainline. Again, the project was abandoned mainly because of the same obstacles as before.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tenders">Tenders</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Tenders">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Samson_tender_Dunge.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Samson_tender_Dunge.JPG/220px-Samson_tender_Dunge.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Samson_tender_Dunge.JPG/330px-Samson_tender_Dunge.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Samson_tender_Dunge.JPG/440px-Samson_tender_Dunge.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Samson_tender_Dunge.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The tender from <i>Hurricane</i> behind <i>Samson</i> at Dungeness</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The following tenders are in use;</p>
<ul>
<li><i>Green Goddess</i> (re-bodied in 2009) and <i>Typhoon</i> (rebodied in 2012) have Ashford 1947 tenders (see below).</li>
<li><i>Northern Chief</i> and <i>Southern Maid</i> ran with 1983–4 built TMA tenders which are similar to, but longer, than the <a href="/wiki/Henry_Greenly" title="Henry Greenly">Greenly</a> tenders and have a greater coal and water capacity. <i>Northern Chief</i> received a new tender tank as part of her overhaul in the winter of 2015. "Southern Maid" will return to traffic in 2016 with a new tender tank which will be a copy of her old tank.</li>
<li><i>The Bug</i>'s tender was newly built in the mid-1970s as the original had been cut up during its time in a Belfast scrap yard.</li>
<li><i>Hercules</i> and <i>Samson</i> have, since 2009, been fitted with new tenders to a design resembling the Great Northern Railway 'high-sided' type.</li>
<li><i>Hurricane</i> is coupled to the re-bodied Paxman-built 1934 large tender, complete with mock corridor connector (a feature of LNER locos used on the non-stop London–Edinburgh services allowing for crew changes en route).</li>
<li><i>Winston Churchill</i> and <i>Doctor Syn</i> have re-bodied Gower tenders using parts from their original Vanderbilt tenders from 1931.</li>
<li><i>Black Prince</i> received a new tender in 2008, using bogies and other parts from its original one which, like the <a href="/wiki/Henry_Greenly" title="Henry Greenly">Greenly</a> tenders, suffered from low water and coal capacity. As built, the loco and tender were fitted with air brakes which were replaced at the RH&amp;DR with vacuum brakes for the loco driving wheels only; the original tender was not altered. The new tender, fitted with vacuum brakes, was tested at New Romney on 27 September 2008. On 4 October 2008, <i>Black Prince</i> completed a 28-mile (45 km) non-stop run from Hythe to Dungeness and back again, without the aid of another tender, a first for this locomotive.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greenly_tenders">Greenly tenders</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Greenly tenders">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Of the seven <a href="/wiki/Henry_Greenly" title="Henry Greenly">Greenly</a> tenders supplied new with locos 1–8, two are still in service albeit with new bodies to the original design. Originally built with vacuum brakes and a handbrake, both brake systems have been removed, leaving them as through-piped only. They were coupled to <i>Hercules</i> and <i>Samson</i> but withdrawn from mainline service due to concerns over safety, and their coal and water capacity.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ashford_tenders">Ashford tenders</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Ashford tenders">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Southern_Railway_(UK)" title="Southern Railway (UK)">Southern Railway</a>'s Ashford works built four tenders in 1946–7. Ashford No 1 ran coupled to <i>Hercules</i>, but was built too high because John Iron, the Southern's draughtsman sent to New Romney to "measure a loco", took his measurements from a Canadian-type Pacific and not a British outline one. The design of subsequent tenders was altered hurriedly after this and the second one, Ashford No 2, was coupled to <i>Typhoon</i>. The design was further refined and two more were constructed. Ashford No 3 was coupled to <i>Green Goddess</i> and Ashford No 4 to <i>Southern Maid</i>. Ashford No 1 last ran in 1974 when <i>Hercules</i> was withdrawn for overhaul. Ashford Nos 2 and 3 are still in service with new bodies. Ashford No 4 was withdrawn when <i>Southern Maid</i> was overhauled in 1983.</p>
<p>Until 1959, when its tender was cut down in size, <i>Hercules</i> ran with the cab roof raised on blocks of wood to match the height of the tender.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tender_shortage">Tender shortage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Tender shortage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Hercules</i> was out of service after the Burmarsh Road level crossing incident in 2003, and <i>Samson</i> was withdrawn from service for an intermediate overhaul shortly afterwards. Once both locomotives were back in service, the railway was faced with a tender shortage. <i>Samson</i> was kept from mainline service while <i>Hercules</i> was coupled to the tender from <i>Green Goddess</i> while it was stored prior to overhaul. During the 2007 season, <i>Samson</i> saw service using the tender from <i>Hurricane</i> while it was being overhauled (a situation that had also happened in 1949 when <i>Samson</i> was used for ballast train duties).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Safety">Safety</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Safety">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Botolph%27s_Bridge_Level_Crossing_on_the_RH%26DR.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="470" data-file-width="630" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Botolph%27s_Bridge_Level_Crossing_on_the_RH%26DR.jpg/220px-Botolph%27s_Bridge_Level_Crossing_on_the_RH%26DR.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Botolph%27s_Bridge_Level_Crossing_on_the_RH%26DR.jpg/330px-Botolph%27s_Bridge_Level_Crossing_on_the_RH%26DR.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Botolph%27s_Bridge_Level_Crossing_on_the_RH%26DR.jpg/440px-Botolph%27s_Bridge_Level_Crossing_on_the_RH%26DR.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Botolph%27s_Bridge_Level_Crossing_on_the_RH%26DR.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The level crossing at Botolph's Bridge was the first to be converted to an ABCL</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway_level_crossing.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Romney%2C_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway_level_crossing.JPG/220px-Romney%2C_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway_level_crossing.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Romney%2C_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway_level_crossing.JPG/330px-Romney%2C_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway_level_crossing.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Romney%2C_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway_level_crossing.JPG/440px-Romney%2C_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway_level_crossing.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway_level_crossing.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hull Road level crossing just south of <a href="/wiki/Romney_Sands_railway_station" title="Romney Sands railway station">Romney Sands</a> before barriers were fitted</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The railway has an exceptionally good safety record,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and all staff (both employed and volunteer) undergo extensive training.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Incidents">Incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There have been a number of serious accidents over the railway's 90 year operation with an extensive mainline timetable. The majority of these have been related to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Level_Crossing" title="Level Crossing">level crossings</a>, and in every documented case the road user has either admitted liability, or been found to have been in the wrong by the subsequent investigation. Despite the presence of large numbers of visitors and tourists, almost all recorded level crossing incidents have involved local car drivers. The more serious incidents, including those at level crossings, have been:</p>
<ul>
<li><b>17 August 1927</b>. 27-year old platelayer Harold Adams was struck and fatally injured by a train whilst he was working on the track near the Prince of Wales Bridge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Snell_1993_1-9"><a href="#cite_note-Snell_1993-1">[1]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>2 June 1931</b>. Locomotive No 10, then still named <i>Doctor Syn</i> (the exchange of names with locomotive No 9 did not take place until later in the year), broke away from its tender, leaving its train near the Coastguard Cottages at Lade. The locomotive continued alone towards Dungeness where the combination of speed, curvature and cant deficiency caused it to derail on the loop and fall on its side. The locomotive was just over two weeks old at the time <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>10 May 1934</b>. A train hauled by the Rolls-Royce locomotive was in collision with a large car at Bonnington Road (since renamed Eastbridge Road) level crossing in Dymchurch. The long-serving internal combustion locomotive (which carried no name at the time of the accident) was derailed and turned on its side, receiving significant damage and narrowly avoiding a fall into the <a href="/wiki/Ditch" title="Ditch">dyke</a> beside the road. The engine driver, Claude Webb, who was also Captain Howey's chauffeur, was slightly injured in the accident. A steam hauled engineers' train was coincidentally nearby at the time, and quickly able to render assistance. The damaged locomotive was sent to <a href="/wiki/Robert_Hudson_(company)" title="Robert Hudson (company)">Robert Hudson Ltd</a> in Leeds for repair, and returned to service later in the same year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>2 September 1935</b>. <i>Northern Chief</i> was struck by a <a href="/wiki/Truck" title="Truck">lorry</a> on the level crossing with Bonnington Road (now known as Eastbridge Road), Dymchurch. The locomotive fell onto its right side coming to rest on the canal bridge. The tender stayed upright. Having sustained minimal damage, the loco was repaired quickly and returned to service. The lorry was a write off.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>16 May 1946</b>. A train hauled by locomotive No 3 <i>Southern Maid</i> was in collision with a lorry at Eastbridge Road level crossing in Dymchurch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> The locomotive was derailed, and fell into the drainage canal running beside the road. The engine driver was badly injured but survived. The lorry driver was killed. The locomotive was recovered from the water by an army crane, but required extensive repairs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>22 April 1947</b>. A train hauled by locomotive No 7 <i>Typhoon</i> was in collision with a large agricultural tractor<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> at an <a href="/wiki/Level_crossing" title="Level crossing">occupation crossing</a> near Prince of Wales, south of Hythe. The subsequent investigation found that the tractor had become stuck on the rails as it had smooth steel wheels, with no spikes, studs or tyres; the tractor driver made no attempt to contact the signalman or warn approaching trains. The engine was derailed and turned on its side, but was not badly damaged and returned to service later the same month. The tractor was split in two and destroyed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>16 July 1952</b>. A head-on collision between two passenger trains (one hauled by No 7 <i>Typhoon</i>, the other by No 8 <i>Hurricane</i>) occurred just north of Britannia Points. The station master at Dungeness, who was not in possession of the single line token, improperly issued the driver of the Up train with a single line ticket and verbally instructed him to take his train to Britannia Points and wait there to be shown the token by the driver of the approaching Down train before proceeding. The Up train over-ran Britannia Points causing the collision.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>11 August 1952</b> The driver of a Down train on the Dungeness line, 21-year-old Jeffery Reddecliffe, was knocked out after striking his head on an overbridge. A passenger in the leading carriage, Leslie J. Ashman, saw this happen, left the carriage, clambered over the tender into the loco cab and stopped the train.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> Captain Howey later presented him with a sea fishing rod in gratitude for his bravery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>2 May 1954</b>. A train driven by Bob Hobbs and hauled by locomotive No 5 <i>Hercules</i> was derailed at half mile curve, between New Romney and Greatstone. The cause of the incident was severe gale-force wind. The train was the 14.50 from Hythe to Dungeness, and the leading vehicle (behind the engine) was a light <a href="/wiki/Brake_van" title="Brake van">guard's van</a>, of a type nicknamed "jumping jacks", as their relatively light weight made for an uncomfortable ride for the guard. In the severe weather, as the train passed over the exposed embankment of half mile curve, the jumping jack guard's van was blown over, and smashed on the embankment. Fortunately the guard, Mavis Thomas, had decided to ride in another coach, and so avoided injury. As the van turned over in the wind, it also tipped the locomotive's high-sided <a href="/wiki/Tender_(rail)" title="Tender (rail)">tender</a>, which in turn tipped the locomotive which ended on its side down the embankment. The engine driver, Bob Hobbs, who was a highly experienced driver, had been alerted to the sequence of events by noises behind him, and was able to jump from the <a href="/wiki/Footplate" title="Footplate">footplate</a>, sustaining only cuts and grazes. All "jumping jack" guard's vans on the railway were withdrawn from service and scrapped.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>27 May 1963</b>. A train hauled by locomotive No 5 <i>Hercules</i> from Hythe to New Romney was suffering from a faulty boiler pressure gauge which was showing erratic readings. The workshop staff at New Romney had recalibrated the safety valves that morning so that they lifted at what the gauge showed as 180 lb sq in. In fact the gauge was reading high. After this the boiler was unable to maintain sufficient pressure to keep the train's vacuum brakes off and they were dragging. The train stalled at Palmarsh, but the driver managed to get it moving again, but at only 3 miles per hour (4.8 km/h). The train was struck from behind by the following service train, hauled by locomotive No 7 <i>Typhoon</i> which had been allowed into the section by the Hythe signalman before he had received line clear from Dymchurch. A number of carriages in both trains were derailed (some telescoped) and there were a number of injuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FH060613_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-FH060613-66">[66]</a></sup> The incident was reported in <a href="/wiki/The_Railway_Magazine" title="The Railway Magazine">The Railway Magazine</a> together with two photographs taken in the aftermath of the crash.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>9 August 1967</b>. A train hauled by locomotive No 5 <i>Hercules</i> driven by Jim Brodie over-ran the terminus at Hythe, resulting in a number of minor injuries. It is thought the engine driver was struck on the head at Prince of Wales Bridge, and lost consciousness, allowing the train to continue unchecked for the remaining <span class="frac nowrap">1<span class="visualhide"> </span><sup>1</sup>⁄<sub>2</sub></span> miles (2.4 km) into Hythe station where it crashed through buffer stops and continued into the station car park, coming to rest before reaching the main road. The driver could not subsequently recall whether his head had struck the stonework of the bridge, or whether he had been hit by an object thrown from the bridge. The incident received national newspaper coverage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>April 1970</b>. A train hauled by locomotive No 2 <i>Northern Chief</i> was in collision with a car at Botolph's Bridge level crossing, south of <a href="/wiki/Palmarsh" title="Palmarsh">Palmarsh</a>. The swift action of the engine driver, Cyril Carter, resulted in a low impact collision, and nobody was injured. The locomotive was slightly damaged. The car, an <a href="/wiki/BMC_ADO16" title="BMC ADO16">Austin 1100</a>, was damaged, but not destroyed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>August 1972</b>. A passenger train was in collision with a circus caravan at St Mary's Road level crossing, Dymchurch. Nobody was injured.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Herald_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-Herald-70">[70]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>6 August 1973</b>. A train hauled by locomotive No 6 <i>Samson</i> was in collision with a stolen motor car at St Mary's Road level crossing, a short distance south of Dymchurch station. The locomotive was badly damaged and the engine driver, Peter Hobson, was killed. The locomotive was sent to Leeds for repair, returning to service the following year. Although not the first level crossing incident on the railway, it was the first to prove fatal to the engine driver, and initiated discussion which led to the gradual introduction of warning lights at all the railway's level crossings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>28 August 1975</b>. A train hauled by locomotive No 7 <i>Typhoon</i> was in collision with a car on St Mary's Road level crossing, Dymchurch. The car, a Ford Corsair, was destroyed, and one of its occupants had to be cut free, having been trapped by her feet, but was not seriously injured. The train driver, Cyril Carter, was uninjured. The occupants of the car were a local young brother and sister, Roger Piper (20) and Belinda Piper (14) driving to the fish and chip shop, and witnesses reported that they had seen the approaching train but tried to race it to the level crossing. Their father John Piper was quoted in the local newspaper as having said, "Funnily enough, it is nearly always someone local who is involved", referring to accidents on Dymchurch's level crossings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Herald_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-Herald-70">[70]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>11 May 1993</b>. A train propelled by locomotive No 12 <i>John Southland</i> driven by Stuart Barratt was in collision with a white van at Eastbridge Road level crossing, Dymchurch. The train was an empty coaching stock (ECS) working which had earlier operated the daily school service for pupils returning home from New Romney. The locomotive was propelling from the rear, and the leading vehicle was <a href="/wiki/Driving_Van_Trailer" title="Driving Van Trailer">Driving Van Trailer</a> (DVT) No 105. The transit van and the railway DVT both fell into the <a href="/wiki/Ditch" title="Ditch">dyke</a> beside the road. The van driver was uninjured. The Guard, Simon Oldfield, who was travelling in the DVT, was briefly trapped under water, but was able to free himself and swim to safety. The DVT was heavily damaged and had to be completely rebuilt. During this rebuild it was adapted to become the railway's first wheelchair accessible coach. Two other passenger coaches, 804 and 807, were also seriously damaged in the incident. The van driver admitted fault but claimed that his brakes had failed. The subsequent police investigation revealed that the brakes had operated correctly, but that the van driver had vainly hoped to beat the train to the crossing. Police also found that the van's tyres were bald, and that it had no current <a href="/wiki/Road_tax" title="Road tax">road tax</a>. A large crane recovered both vehicles from the water.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>3 August 2003</b>. A train hauled by locomotive No 5 <i>Hercules</i> was in collision with a car at Burmarsh Road level crossing protected by flashing warning lights.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> The engine driver, 31-year-old Kevin Crouch, died at the scene, and some passengers were treated for shock and minor injuries. The locomotive was seriously damaged and underwent extensive repairs, returning to service in 2005. The female car driver, 22-year old Marie Scrace<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> whose baby was a passenger in the vehicle, had ignored or failed to see the warning lights. Scrace and her baby were taken to hospital, but were not badly hurt. The railway and the <a href="/wiki/Health_and_Safety_Executive" title="Health and Safety Executive">Health and Safety Executive</a> instigated an investigation, and the woman was arrested on suspicion of causing death by dangerous driving. Although acquitted, she was found guilty of the lesser charge of careless driving.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>10 July 2005</b>. A train hauled by locomotive No 8 <i>Hurricane</i> was in collision with a car at Battery Road level crossing near Dungeness. The driver of the train, Suzanne Martin (the wife of the railway's general manager), was killed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc2005_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc2005-77">[77]</a></sup> Several passengers were treated for shock. The locomotive was seriously damaged and underwent extensive repairs, returning to service the following year. The car driver, 20-year old Richard Isted, had ignored or failed to see warning lights and was arrested at the scene by Kent Police. He subsequently appeared in court charged with driving without due care and attention, to which he pleaded guilty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>10 September 2016</b>. A passenger train was struck by a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Agricultural_tractor" title="Agricultural tractor">tractor</a> pulling a heavily laden hay trailer, on occupation crossing number 10 (approximately half a mile north of Dymchurch station). Locomotive No 1 <i>Green Goddess</i> and its tender were both derailed and thrown onto their sides. The leading coach was also derailed but remained upright. The train driver and four passengers sustained minor injuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KM102447_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-KM102447-79">[79]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Level_crossings">Level crossings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Level crossings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Following the two fatal accidents in 2003 and 2005, the railway began a programme of level crossing refurbishment. There are a number of occupation crossings with local control, where the railway meets farm tracks, but of the eighteen junctions of the railway with public highways, five are road bridges and the other thirteen are level crossings. During the late 1970s to early 1980s, all thirteen had been converted to automatic open crossings (AOCLs)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-orr_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-orr-80">[80]</a></sup> by installation of flashing warning lights. Between 2006 and 2016, twelve of them were upgraded to Automatic Barrier Crossing Locally Monitored (ABCL) status. This involved the decommissioning of the life expired AOCL control equipment, the installation of lifting half-barriers and totally new control and train detection systems, at a cost of around £90,000 per crossing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc2005_77-1"><a href="#cite_note-bbc2005-77">[77]</a></sup>) On 22nd of March 2017 the crossing at Romney Sands was commissioned as an ABCL, this means that all the 13 crossings on the line have barriers and it brought the level crossing upgrade program to a close. During the single line crossing upgrades the Road Signal heads (Wig Wags) have either been replaced with new ones (Battery Road and Dungeness Road) or had their existing heads refurbished.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ownership_and_operation">Ownership and operation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Ownership and operation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ownership">Ownership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Ownership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The railway is owned by <b>Romney, Hythe &amp; Dymchurch Railway PLC</b>, which was originally incorporated as a private limited company on 15 November 1971 under the name RH&amp;D Light Railway Holding Company Limited, adopting its present title on re-registration as a "new" <a href="/wiki/Public_limited_company" title="Public limited company">public limited company</a> under Section 8(3) of the Companies Act 1980 on 10 May 1982.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> Its shareholders (of whom there are now over a thousand) travel free of charge on trains, but receive no financial dividend on their shareholdings, instead re-investing all operating profit back into the company. At 14 June 2015 there were 25 "Gold Medallion" shareholders owning 5,000 or more shares each and 119 "Silver Medallion" shareholders owning between 500 and 4,999 shares each. The remaining shareholders owned between 100 and 499 shares each. The PLC's issued and fully paid share capital at that date was £508,858 in £1 Ordinary Shares.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>Shares in the PLC remain available to the public at a cost of £4 each. The minimum holding is 100 shares, but above this number potential shareholders may purchase any amount. Further details can be obtained from the Company Secretary, Romney, Hythe &amp; Dymchurch Railway PLC, New Romney Station, New Romney, Kent TN28 8PL.</p>
<p>The two largest shareholders in the PLC are the Romney, Hythe &amp; Dymchurch Railway Association with 78,604 shares (15.45%) and Sir William McAlpine Bt (leader of the "consortium" which saved the railway from closure in 1972) who holds 38,837 (7.63%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_82-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-82">[82]</a></sup> The PLC controls the entire share capital of the older statutory Romney, Hythe &amp; Dymchurch Light Railway Company, incorporated by The Romney, Hythe &amp; Dymchurch Light Railway Order 1926. It acquired a controlling interest in the Statutory Company on 14 February 1972 for £106,947.64 when it purchased 50,447 of the 51,000 Statutory Company shares then in issue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Snell_1993_1-10"><a href="#cite_note-Snell_1993-1">[1]</a></sup> Since February 1972 it has bought out all of the minority shareholders in the Statutory Company which is now a wholly owned subsidiary.</p>
<p>The Romney, Hythe &amp; Dymchurch Light Railway (Amendment) Order 1974<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SI1974_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-SI1974-83">[83]</a></sup> altered the capital structure of the Statutory Company, allowing its issued share capital and borrowings to amount in aggregate to £400,000 (instead of the previously completely inadequate £68,000). On 1 October 1975 the Statutory Company created a further 24,000 new shares, bringing its issued capital up to £75,000 in £1 shares. The PLC subscribed for 23,950 of these new shares and the remaining 50 were acquired by a director of the Statutory Company in order to bring their holding up to the minimum for directors of 250 shares specified in the 1926 Light Railway Order.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> Directors' shareholdings in the Statutory Company are subject to rights of pre-emption by the PLC and are therefore treated for most purposes as being owned by that company.</p>
<p>It is usual for the two companies to share the same board of directors; with the anomaly that whilst the Romney, Hythe &amp; Dymchurch Railway Association has been granted a seat on the Statutory Company's board it has no direct representation on the PLC's board.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Directors">Directors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Directors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Romney, Hythe &amp; Dymchurch Light Railway Order 1926 <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> restricted the maximum number of directors of the Statutory Company to five and named Captain John Edwards Presgrave Howey, Gladys May Howey, Captain John Alexander Holder, Major William Bertram Bell and Henry Greenly as the first directors. Greenly never owned more than 50 shares in the company so was ineligible to sit on the board and Holder did not achieve the qualifying holding of 250 shares until 30 December 1929.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Snell_1993_1-11"><a href="#cite_note-Snell_1993-1">[1]</a></sup> Gladys Howey was also ineligible until 1931 when her shareholding reached 250 and she was able to join the board.</p>
<p>Section 5 of The Romney, Hythe &amp; Dymchurch Light Railway (Amendment) Order 1974 <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SI1974_83-1"><a href="#cite_note-SI1974-83">[83]</a></sup> increased the maximum number of directors from five to 10 and also set the minimum number of directors at three.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Operation">Operation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Operation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The day-to-day operation of the railway is in the hands of a full-time permanent staff of around 35 assisted by 5 part-time permanent staff.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> These include a General Manager, departmental managers (engineering, commercial and operations) and a large number of engineering staff (from locomotive fitters to permanent way gangers) and catering staff (the New Romney and Dungeness cafes and the Light Railway Restaurant adjoining Hythe station are open all year round; some of the railway's other commercial outlets are more seasonal). In addition to this core staff, seasonal employees are taken on through the summer season, particularly to increase the staffing of the shops and catering outlets and to provide the required levels of staffing at stations. At the height of the operating season there are over 60 staff on the payroll.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Snell_1993_1-12"><a href="#cite_note-Snell_1993-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>The railway depends upon a dedicated team of fully trained but unpaid volunteer staff members who work on the railway in their own spare time. Volunteer staff work throughout the railway, in engineering posts, operating positions, commercial outlets, and manual roles concerned with maintenance and improvement.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Romney,_Hythe_and_Dymchurch_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
